###begin article-title 0
###xml 102 108 102 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CDKN1A</italic>
###xml 158 159 154 155 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 159 160 155 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn1">*</xref>
###xml 160 162 156 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn3">S&#8414;</xref>
Cyclical Chromatin Looping and Transcription Factor Association on the Regulatory Regions of the p21 (CDKN1A) Gene in Response to 1alpha,25-Dihydroxyvitamin D3*Sâƒž
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 213 236 213 236 <email xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">carsten.carlberg@uni.lu</email>
 To whom correspondence should be addressed: Life Sciences Research Unit, Universite du Luxembourg, 162A, Ave. de la Faiencerie, L-1511 Luxembourg, Luxembourg. Tel.: 352-466644-6267; Fax: 352-466644-6435; E-mail: carsten.carlberg@uni.lu. 
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>
Author's Choice
###end p 2
###begin p 3
 applies to Author Choice Articles
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 144 150 144 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CDKN1A</italic>
###xml 152 155 152 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 272 273 268 269 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 402 405 398 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 452 455 448 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1120 1123 1116 1119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1499 1500 1491 1492 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1511 1514 1503 1506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
The nuclear receptor vitamin D receptor (VDR) is known to associate with three vitamin D response element (VDREs)-containing regions within the CDKN1A (p21) gene region. Here we show in MDA-MB453 breast cancer cells that the natural VDR ligand 1alpha,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 causes cyclical transcription factor binding and chromatin looping of distal VDREs to the transcription start site (TSS) of the p21 gene, leading to cyclical accumulation of the p21 mRNA. At the chromatin level, association of the mediator protein MED1 precedes both the peaks of VDR binding to VDREs and phosphorylated RNA polymerase (p-Pol II) to the TSS. The loss of co-repressor NCoR1-histone deacetylase (HDAC) 3 complex and inhibitory chromatin looping from VDREs to the TSS are also initial events followed by increased acetylation of histone 3 at lysine 9 at the TSS prior to initiation of transcription. Simultaneous to VDR and p-Pol II peaks, chromatin loops between VDREs and the TSS are formed, and the lysine demethylase LSD1 and the histone acetyltransferase CBP are enriched in both regions. This is followed by a moderate peak in p21 transcript accumulation, repeated in cycles of 45-60 min. The transcript accumulation pattern is disturbed by siRNA inhibition of the mediator protein MED1, LSD1, NCoR1, or various HDACs, whereas CBP appears unnecessary for the response. Inhibition of MED1, HDAC4, or LSD1 by siRNA also attenuates ligand-induced chromatin looping. In conclusion, 1alpha,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 regulates p21 transcription by inducing cyclical chromatin looping that depends on both histone deacetylation and demethylation.
###end p 4

###begin p 7
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>
Author's Choice-Final version full access.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 40 41 40 41 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn4">2</xref>
###xml 222 223 222 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref1">1</xref>
###xml 277 278 273 274 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 293 294 285 286 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 295 296 287 288 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 400 401 392 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref2">2</xref>
###xml 513 514 501 502 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 515 516 503 504 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 549 550 537 538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref3">3</xref>
###xml 656 657 640 641 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 658 659 642 643 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 787 788 771 772 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 860 861 840 841 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 862 863 842 843 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 943 949 923 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CDKN1A</italic>
###xml 963 966 943 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1026 1027 1006 1007 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 1125 1128 1105 1108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1135 1136 1115 1116 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
As a member of the nuclear receptor (NR)2 superfamily the vitamin D receptor (VDR) acts as a transcription factor that binds to specific response elements (VDREs) within the regulatory regions of its primary target genes (1). The natural VDR ligand 1alpha,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 (1alpha,25(OH)2D3) has an important role in the regulation of calcium and phosphate homeostasis and bone mineralization (2). In addition to this classical role, there is both epidemiological and preclinical evidence that 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 is an anti-proliferative agent (3). Vitamin D deficiency increases the risk of certain cancers, whereas the administration of 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 in cell culture or in animal models for cancer inhibits angiogenesis and induces G0/G1 arrest, differentiation, and apoptosis (4). These anti-proliferative effects are exerted by various 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 target genes, among which the product of cyclin-dependent kinase inhibitor 1A (CDKN1A, also called p21) gene induces G0/G1 cell cycle arrest and differentiation (5). We have previously characterized three functional VDREs residing 2-7-kb upstream of the TSS of p21 gene (6).
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 454 455 454 455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref7">7</xref>
Non-liganded VDR is associated with primary co-repressors, such as the nuclear receptor co-repressor (NCoR1), that attenuate transcription via interaction with histone deacetylases (HDACs) that pose the chromatin modifications unfavorable for transcription or, at least in the case of NCoR1, are also able to recruit a H2A ubiquitin ligase that inhibits the elongation by RNA polymerase II (Pol II) beyond the first nucleosome of the transcribed region (7).
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 184 185 184 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref1">1</xref>
Introduction of a ligand results in a conformational change in the ligand-binding domain of the VDR, leading to enhanced binding to its heterodimerization partner retinoid X receptor (1) and an exchange of co-repressors to primary co-activators. Those include the members of the p160 family that recruit secondary co-activators, such as the histone-modifying enzymes, the histone acetyltransferase CBP, and the lysine demethylase LSD1, and the mediator complex subunit MED1 that enables the contact to transcriptional machinery.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 274 275 274 275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 408 409 408 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref9">9</xref>
###xml 520 522 520 522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref10">10</xref>
###xml 640 642 640 642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref11">11</xref>
###xml 644 646 644 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
The histone modifications serve as specific signals for chromatin-binding proteins, affecting cofactors that remodel the chromatin to permit transcription. For example, dimethylation of histone 3 at lysine 4 (H3K4me2) is linked to active core promoter and enhancer regions (8) and is recognized by the ATP-dependent chromatin-remodeling factor CHD1 that can alter the accessibility of DNA for transcription (9). Acetylated histone 3 at lysine 9 (H3K9ac) has a strong association to positive regulation of transcription (10) and is recognized by CBP that acetylates H3K14 and TAF1, which a subunit of the general transcription factor TFIID (11, 12).
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 242 244 242 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref13">13</xref>
###xml 620 621 613 614 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 622 623 615 616 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 625 627 618 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref14">14</xref>
###xml 628 630 621 623 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
In addition to providing a contact between sequence-specific transcription factors and the basal transcription machinery, the Mediator complex promotes the formation of the preinitiation complex and the phosphorylation of Pol II at serine 5 (13). As VDREs are not restricted to proximal promoters of VDR target genes, chromatin looping provides the physical proximity between the response element and the TSS. Stimulus-dependent changes in chromatin looping have been studied extensively in the beta-globin locus at different stages of development, but also in response to NR ligands, such as estradiol and 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 (14-17).
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 163 165 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>
###xml 202 204 198 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>
###xml 207 213 203 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">GADD45</italic>
###xml 219 224 215 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">VDUP1</italic>
###xml 232 234 228 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref20">20</xref>
Recently, cyclical models have been proposed for the activation of transcription by NRs, including those for estrogen receptor alpha on the trefoil factor-1 gene (18) and for VDR on the 24-hydroxylase (19), GADD45, and VDUP1 genes (20). In these models the ligand-dependent transcription is seen as a cyclical process, where alternating activating and repressive actions on chromatin are required, providing means to stringently regulate the endurance and strength of the transcriptional response.
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 249 252 249 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 472 473 468 469 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 474 475 470 471 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 648 651 644 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 812 815 808 811 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 994 997 990 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1026 1027 1018 1019 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1028 1029 1020 1021 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
To investigate the interactive transcriptional role of NRs and chromatin looping, we studied protein-chromatin associations on both the VDREs and the TSS, the association frequency between the TSS and the VDREs as well as the outcome in the form of p21 transcript accumulation. The role of histone-modifying cofactors along with the mediator complex subunit MED1 in the latter two processes was also investigated by siRNA knock-down. After synchronization by 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 alone, we observed that the ligand induces cyclical mRNA accumulation, chromatin looping and association of p-Pol II, MED1, and VDR with the VDRE containing regions of the p21 promoter. Furthermore, MED1, HDAC4, and LSD1 were found to be essential for ligand-dependent looping from distal regions to the TSS and the cyclic induction of p21 transcription. In conclusion, both histone deacetylation and demethylation are essential for the ligand-dependent dynamic looping of chromatin and the increased transcription of p21 in response to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3.
###end p 14
###begin title 15
EXPERIMENTAL PROCEDURES
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 0 12 0 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cell Culture</italic>
###xml 169 170 165 166 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 649 650 633 634 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 664 665 644 645 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 666 667 646 647 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 23 28 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 127 133 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 388 394 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Cell Culture-MDA-MB453 human mammary epithelial metastatic carcinoma cells were grown in alpha-MEM supplemented with 10% fetal bovine serum in a humidified 95% air/5% CO2 incubator. Before mRNA extraction, 650,000 cells for each well of a 6-well plate were seeded approximately24 h prior to collection in phenol red-free Dulbecco's modified Eagle's medium with 5% charcoal-stripped fetal bovine serum. For chromatin immunoprecipitation (ChIP) assay or chromosome conformation capture (3C) assay, cells were grown in the same medium overnight to reach 50 to 60% confluency. For all experiments, cells were treated for indicated time periods with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 (kindly provided by Dr. Milan Uskokovic, BioXell Inc, Nutley, NJ) or ethanol (0.001%).
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 0 45 0 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RNA Extraction and Real-time Quantitative PCR</italic>
###xml 126 128 126 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 510 571 484 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CBP, HDAC3, HDAC4, HDAC5, HDAC7, LSD1, MED1, NCoR1, p21, SMRT</italic>
###xml 617 622 591 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RPLP0</italic>
###xml 712 727 686 693 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">-(&#916;&#916;Ct)</sup>
###xml 762 770 716 724 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(ligand)</sub>
###xml 778 787 728 737 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(vehicle)</sub>
###xml 803 806 749 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 803 806 749 752 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>p21</italic></sub>
###xml 813 818 759 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RPLP0</italic>
###xml 813 818 759 764 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>RPLP0</italic></sub>
RNA Extraction and Real-time Quantitative PCR-Total RNA extraction and cDNA synthesis were performed as described previously (17). Real-time quantitative PCR for cDNA was performed using a LightCycler(R) 480 System (Roche Applied Science) and FastStart SYBR Green Master mix (Roche Applied Science). The PCR cycling conditions were: preincubation for 10 min at 95 degreesC, 38 cycles of 20 s at 95 degreesC, 15 s at 60 degreesC and 15 s at 72 degreesC. The sequences of the specific primer pairs for the genes CBP, HDAC3, HDAC4, HDAC5, HDAC7, LSD1, MED1, NCoR1, p21, SMRT, and the control gene acidic riboprotein P0 (RPLP0) are listed in supplemental Table S1. Fold inductions were calculated using the formula 2-(DeltaDeltaCt), where DeltaDeltaCt is the DeltaCt(ligand)-DeltaCt(vehicle), DeltaCt is Ct(p21) - Ct(RPLP0) and Ct is the cycle at which the threshold is crossed. Quality of the PCR product was monitored using post-PCR melt curve analysis.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 0 10 0 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ChIP Assay</italic>
###xml 68 69 68 69 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 642 643 636 637 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 665 666 659 660 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1087 1089 1075 1077 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
###xml 481 487 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
ChIP Assay-ChIP and re-ChIP were performed as described previously (6) except for the following changes: (i) formaldehyde cross-linking time was reduced to 5 min, (ii) chromatin was lysed in 0.6 ml (instead of 1 ml) and sonicated using a Bioruptor UCD-200 (Diagenode, Liege, Belgium) with 10 x 30 s pulses, (iii) preincubation with salmon sperm beads was left out and instead protein A-agarose beads (Upstate Biotechnology, Lake Placid, NY) were blocked overnight with 10 mg/ml of bovine serum albumin and 0.1 mg/ml of salmon sperm DNA at 4 degreesC, and (iv) chromatin bound to agarose beads were eluted with a different elution buffer (25 mm Tris-HCl pH 7.5, 10 mm EDTA, 0.5% SDS) for 30 min at 65 degreesC followed by second elution for 2 min at room temperature. Antibodies against VDR (sc-1008), HDAC3 (sc-11417), HDAC4 (sc-11418), CBP (sc-369), NCoR1 (sc-8994), and p53 (sc-6243) were obtained from Santa Cruz Biotechnologies (Santa Cruz, CA). The antibody against p53 was used as a negative control because in MDA-MB453 cells the DNA binding domain of the p53 protein is mutated (21). Antibodies against H3K4me2 (07-030) and H3K9ac (07-352) were obtained from Upstate, while antibodies against the phosphorylated Pol II (p-Pol II; ab5131), LSD1 (ab17721) and T1457-phosphorylated MED1 (ab60950) were obtained from Abcam (Cambridge, UK).
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3C Assay</italic>
###xml 347 348 345 346 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 361 362 359 360 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 400 401 398 399 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 772 773 764 765 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 958 959 950 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 1006 1009 998 1001 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
3C Assay-Chromatin from two cells of a 6-well plate (750,000 cells plated per well) was collected, cross-linked, and lysed as for ChIP assays, but the sonication was reduced to one 15-s pulse. After removal of cellular debris by centrifugation, 25 mul of chromatin was diluted in 75 mul of ChIP dilution buffer (0.01% SDS, 1.1% Triton X-100, 1.2 mm EDTA, 16.7 mm NaCl, protease inhibitors, and 16.7 mm Tris-HCl, pH 8.1) supplemented with protease inhibitors (Complete protease inhibitor mixture, Roche Applied Science), Red or Tango buffer (Fermentas, Vilnius, Lithuania) and digested overnight at 37 degreesC with 25 units of the restriction enzymes MvaI or Hpy8I (Fermentas), respectively. Digested chromatin was diluted 1:6 to T4 ligation buffer supplemented with 0.5 mm ATP and ligated with 15 units of T4 DNA ligase (Fermentas) for 4 h at room temperature. Samples were reverse cross-linked and DNA was recovered as described previously for ChIP assay (6). As positive controls, plasmids carrying the p21 promoter regions-7930 to -6072 or -4968 to +37 were digested and ligated with plasmid covering the TSS region (-676 to +535).
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 0 26 0 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">PCR of Chromatin Templates</italic>
###xml 90 93 90 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 609 611 609 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 1382 1392 1344 1350 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">-(&#916;Ct)</sup>
###xml 1413 1421 1367 1375 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(output)</sub>
###xml 1426 1433 1380 1387 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(input)</sub>
###xml 1630 1631 1584 1585 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">-</sup>
###xml 1632 1644 1586 1590 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;&#916;Ct</sup>
###xml 1680 1688 1614 1622 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(target)</sub>
###xml 1710 1713 1640 1643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1748 1751 1678 1681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1697 1783 1627 1713 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(non-treated <italic>p21</italic>-2 for Hpy8Irestricted template or <italic>p21</italic>-3 for MvaI restricted template)</sub>
###xml 1799 1801 1725 1727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3C</italic>
###xml 1798 1819 1724 1745 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(<italic>3C</italic> ligation product)</sub>
###xml 1825 1849 1751 1775 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">positive control plasmid</italic>
###xml 1824 1850 1750 1776 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(<italic>positive control plasmid</italic>)</sub>
PCR of Chromatin Templates-For each of the three VDRE-carrying regions and the TSS of the p21 gene, genomic primers were designed (supplemental Table S2) and for their quantification 6-carboxyfluorescein (FAM)-modified probes were used (supplemental Table S3). Similarly, primers were designed for the detection of C3 ligation products (supplemental Table S4) and their TaqMan quantification (supplemental Table S5). To achieve quantifiable product specificity, the probes used for 3C ligation products were targeted against the ligation site, as described previously for quantification of chromatin looping (16). All oligonucleotides used in this study were obtained from Eurogentec (Liege, Belgium). Real-time quantitative PCR was performed with the Maxima Probe qPCR master mix (Fermentas) on a LightCycler(R) 480 System (Roche). The PCR cycling conditions were: preincubation for 10 min at 95 degreesC, 50 cycles of 20 s at 95 degreesC, 60 s at 60 degreesC. For the PCR on the TSS, preincubation for 10 min at 95 degreesC, 50 cycles of 20 s at 95 degreesC, 60 s at 61 degreesC was used with GC-rich solution (Roche Applied Science) in addition to the Maxima Probe qPCR master mix. The PCR products were also resolved on 2% agarose gels to control correct product size. Relative association of chromatin-bound proteins or histone modifications were calculated using the formula 2-(DeltaCt), where DeltaCt is Ct(output) - Ct(input), output is the immunoprecipitated DNA and input is the purified genomic DNA from starting material of the ChIP assay. For the 3C assay relative chromatin looping was calculated using the formula 2-(DeltaDeltaCt), where DeltaDeltaCt is the DeltaCt(target) -DeltaCt(non-treated p21-2 for Hpy8Irestricted template or p21-3 for MvaI restricted template), DeltaCt is Ct(3C ligation product) - Ct(positive control plasmid).
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 1.</label>
###xml 31 34 31 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 9 53 9 53 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cyclical induction of <italic>p21</italic> transcription by 1</bold>
###xml 66 67 62 63 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>

###xml 165 168 161 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 218 219 214 215 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>

###xml 670 671 662 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 9 681 9 673 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="22"><bold>Cyclical induction of <italic>p21</italic> transcription by 1</bold>&#945;<bold>,25,(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub>.</bold> Real-time quantitative PCR was performed to measure the time-dependent mRNA expression of the <italic>p21</italic> gene in MDA-MB453 cells after treatment with 10 n<sc>m</sc> 1&#945;,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub>. The data were normalized to the expression of the housekeeping gene <italic>RPLP0</italic>, and fold inductions were calculated in reference to vehicle control. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's <italic>t</italic> test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (<sup>*</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.05; <sup>**</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.01; <sup>***</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.001).</p>

FIGURE 1.Cyclical induction of p21 transcription by 1alpha,25,(OH)2D3. Real-time quantitative PCR was performed to measure the time-dependent mRNA expression of the p21 gene in MDA-MB453 cells after treatment with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3. The data were normalized to the expression of the housekeeping gene RPLP0, and fold inductions were calculated in reference to vehicle control. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's t test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (*, p < 0.05; **, p < 0.01; ***, p < 0.001).
###end p 21

Cyclical induction of p21 transcription by 1alpha,25,(OH)2D3. Real-time quantitative PCR was performed to measure the time-dependent mRNA expression of the p21 gene in MDA-MB453 cells after treatment with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3. ###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">siRNA Inhibition</italic>
siRNA Inhibition-MDA-MB453 cells were reverse transfected with Lipofectamine RNAiMAX (Invitrogen, Carlsbad, CA) according to the manufacturer's instructions using a mixture of three double-stranded siRNA oligonucleotides per gene (Eurogentec, 200 pmol of each siRNA, supplemental Table S6). For cDNA synthesis 650,000 cells, for 3C assays 750,000 cells, and for ChIP assays 4,500,000 cells were used. Cell treatments were started 24 h after plating and RNA extraction, real-time quantitative PCR, ChIP assays, and 3C assays were carried out as described above.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
RESULTS
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 0 46 0 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cyclical Induction of p21 mRNA Expression by 1</italic>
###xml 58 59 54 55 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 60 61 56 57 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 51 61 47 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub></italic>
###xml 66 69 62 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 117 118 109 110 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 119 120 111 112 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 179 181 171 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 221 224 213 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 288 291 280 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 336 337 324 325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 338 339 326 327 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 400 406 388 394 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1</xref>
###xml 427 430 415 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 641 644 629 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 684 687 672 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 714 717 702 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 989 990 973 974 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 991 992 975 976 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1060 1063 1044 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
Cyclical Induction of p21 mRNA Expression by 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-The p21 gene has been shown to respond to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 in several mammary cell lines, including MDA-MB453 cells (17). To further elucidate the dynamics of p21 induction, we performed real-time quantitative PCR analysis of p21 mRNA expression in response to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 in a detailed time course of 300 min with 15-min intervals (Fig. 1). The first peak of p21 mRNA expression appeared after 60 min, the second at 105 min followed by a third at 150 min. A fourth peak appeared at 210 min and a fifth peak at 255 to 270 min. After each of these peaks, the accumulation of p21 mRNA ceased resulting in a decrease of p21 mRNA levels. The peaks of p21 mRNA levels appeared in cycles of 45-60 min with the longest lag time after the major peak at 150 min, where a 1.7-fold induction decreased within 45 min to levels close to that of untreated cells. Please note that the cells had not been synchronized. Thus, 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 in itself seems to be sufficient for the induction of cyclicity in p21 transcription.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 61 62 57 58 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 63 64 59 60 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 73 76 69 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
Taken together, these observations suggest that 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 induces p21 transcription only for short periods at selected time points. Moreover, the drastic decreases of the transcript accumulation level between the phases of mRNA induction indicate that the gene is actively repressed at these time points.
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 0 51 0 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cyclical Enrichment of VDR, p-Pol II, and MED1 on 1</italic>
###xml 63 64 59 60 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 65 66 61 62 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 56 85 52 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub>-responsive Regions</italic>
###xml 133 136 129 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 170 171 162 163 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 172 173 164 165 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 281 284 273 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 320 321 308 309 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 322 323 310 311 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 458 464 446 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 522 525 510 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 551 557 539 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1</xref>
###xml 648 649 632 633 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 650 651 634 635 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 730 731 714 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 733 735 717 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 745 748 729 732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 801 802 785 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 795 802 779 786 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>A</italic></xref>
Cyclical Enrichment of VDR, p-Pol II, and MED1 on 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-responsive Regions-To study whether the cyclical induction of the p21 mRNA in response to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 is based on parallel cyclical association of VDR and its partner proteins to the regulatory regions of the p21 gene, we performed in 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-treated MDA-MB453 cells ChIP assays with antibodies against VDR, p-Pol II, MED1, HDAC3, HDAC4, CBP, NCoR1, H3K4me2, H3K9ac, and LSD1 (Fig. 2). We analyzed the time period 0 to 150 min, in which the p21 mRNA peaked three times (Fig. 1). On the chromatin templates we determined by real-time quantitative PCR the 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-induced enrichment of the three previously identified VDR-associated regions (6, 17) and the p21 TSS in comparison to that in untreated cells (Fig. 2A).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 43 44 39 40 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 45 46 41 42 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 198 199 194 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 192 199 188 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 278 287 274 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-1, -2</italic>
###xml 293 295 289 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">-3</italic>
###xml 457 461 453 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i.e.</italic>
###xml 712 713 708 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 718 719 714 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 704 719 700 715 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2, <italic>B</italic> and <italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 915 916 911 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 909 916 905 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 971 975 967 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i.e.</italic>
###xml 1375 1380 1371 1376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-1</italic>
Because the central events of 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-dependent gene transcription are the direct binding of VDR and the induction of transcription by Pol II, these two proteins were analyzed first (Fig. 2B). The association of VDR peaked at all three VDRE containing genomic regions (p21-1, -2, and -3) at 30-45, 90, and 150 min after the onset of ligand treatment. Similar pattern with the same maxima was observed also for p-Pol II. However, already at 15 min, i.e. before VDR and p-Pol II peaks, acetylation of H3K9 was induced 2-fold on the TSS. Similarly, MED1 peaked at 15 min on regions 1 and 2, HDAC3 decreased on all regions, whereas NCoR1 was significantly decreased only on the TSS and on region 3 (Fig. 2, B and C). It should be noted that the basal levels of H3K4me2 and H3K9ac were 20- and 3-times higher, respectively, on the TSS than on the VDRE-containing regions. Therefore, they are presented in Fig. 2C in separated graphs with different scales. At 30 min, i.e. together with VDR and p-Pol II, MED1 peaked at the TSS and on region 3, CBP on the TSS and H3K9ac on regions 1 and 2. Simultaneously, H3K4me2 was induced on all regions, and LSD1 on regions 2, 3, and the TSS. After 45 min of treatment, the enrichment of VDR still peaked on regions 1 and 3 and levels of p-Pol II remained higher than in untreated cells, whereas MED1 escaped from the TSS and region p21-1. Concurrently, the enrichment of H3K4me2 and H3K9ac were reduced on the TSS. At the time point 60 min, most proteins displayed low associations, while MED1 showed a minor peak on region 3.
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 2.</label>
###xml 120 123 120 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>

###xml 162 165 162 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 230 231 230 231 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 266 267 266 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 428 429 428 429 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 443 444 439 440 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 445 446 441 442 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 472 473 468 469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 478 479 474 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>

Association of p53 was subtracted from relative association levels to control for nonspecific binding. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's <italic>t</italic> test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (<sup>*</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.05; <sup>**</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.01; <sup>***</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.001).</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="zbc014096885002a"/><graphic xlink:href="zbc014096885002b"/></fig>
###xml 156 161 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
FIGURE 2.Dynamic association of VDR, cofactors, and histone modifications to VDRE containing regions and the TSS of the p21 gene. Schematic overview on the human p21 promoter indicating the location of VDREs described previously (6) and of targeted genomic regions (A). On each of these four regions ChIP assays with indicated antibodies were performed on chromatin extracted from MDA-MB453 cells that had been treated with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 for the indicated times (B and C). Analysis was performed by real-time quantitative PCR using FAM-labeled probes, and association was calculated relative to input samples. Association of p53 was subtracted from relative association levels to control for nonspecific binding. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's t test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (*, p < 0.05; **, p < 0.01; ***, p < 0.001).
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 111 114 111 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 0 120 0 120 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Dynamic association of VDR, cofactors, and histone modifications to VDRE containing regions and the TSS of the <italic>p21</italic> gene.</bold>
###xml 153 156 153 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 221 222 221 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 257 258 257 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 419 420 419 420 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 434 435 430 431 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 436 437 432 433 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 463 464 459 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 469 470 465 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 858 859 854 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 969 970 965 966 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">*</sup>
###xml 972 973 968 969 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 982 984 978 980 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">**</sup>
###xml 986 987 982 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 996 999 992 995 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">***</sup>
###xml 1001 1002 997 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 147 152 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Dynamic association of VDR, cofactors, and histone modifications to VDRE containing regions and the TSS of the p21 gene. Schematic overview on the human p21 promoter indicating the location of VDREs described previously (6) and of targeted genomic regions (A). On each of these four regions ChIP assays with indicated antibodies were performed on chromatin extracted from MDA-MB453 cells that had been treated with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 for the indicated times (B and C). Analysis was performed by real-time quantitative PCR using FAM-labeled probes, and association was calculated relative to input samples. Association of p53 was subtracted from relative association levels to control for nonspecific binding. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's t test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (*, p < 0.05; **, p < 0.01; ***, p < 0.001).
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 43 47 43 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i.e.</italic>
At 90 min after onset of ligand treatment, i.e. concurrently with the second peak of VDR and p-Pol II association, MED1 and HDAC3 peaked on region 1, H3K9ac on both regions 1 and 2, CBP on region 3, and LSD1 on region 2. In contrast, NCoR1 stayed low on all regions, while HDAC4 increased only on region 1. At 120 min the rather low association of VDR and p-Pol II with all regions was well reflected by MED1, while HDAC3 and HDAC4 were still high on region 1, CBP on region 3, and NCoR1 on all regions. In addition, H3K4me2 was high on region 3, whereas H3K9ac was reduced from the TSS. Finally, the third peak of VDR and p-Pol II at 150 min coincided with increased binding of MED1 to the TSS, H3K9ac of the TSS and NCoR1 binding to region 1.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 455 456 451 452 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 457 458 453 454 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 491 494 487 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 536 543 532 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
In summary, VDR and p-Pol II binding patterns showed similarity to each other on all regions studied, as well as to the patterns of MED1 and LSD1 association. H3K9ac displayed analogy to VDR, p-Pol II and MED1 association. Unlike other enrichments studied, those of H3K4me2 and HDAC4 did not show cyclicity. Generally, the effects on histone modifications and protein association were modest but significant, reflecting the modest effects of 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 on the transcript levels of the p21 gene. All observations are summarized in Table 1.
###end p 32

###begin p 35
###xml 13 14 9 10 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>

1alpha,25(OH)2D3-triggered associations of proteins with four regions of the p21 promoter are summarized and compared with histone modifications, looping to the TSS and mRNA accumulation. "+" indicates a region showing significantly increased association with the mentioned protein/looping to the TSS compared to untreated cells. At the time 0 point, this indicates that the region shows significantly higher association with the mentioned protein/looping to the TSS compared to the lowest point in treated cells, "-" indicates regions showing significantly decreased association with the mentioned protein/looping to the TSS compared to untreated cells, whereas blank entries represent no significant change.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 0 77 0 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Dynamic Chromatin Looping Provides a Contact between VDRE Regions and the TSS</italic>
###xml 231 234 231 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 274 280 274 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3</xref>
###xml 839 842 839 842 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 967 969 967 969 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref22">22</xref>
###xml 1211 1214 1211 1214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1280 1281 1280 1281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1274 1281 1274 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>A</italic></xref>
Dynamic Chromatin Looping Provides a Contact between VDRE Regions and the TSS-To unravel the spatial requirements as to how the VDRE carrying regions up to 7-kb upstream of the TSS harvest p-Pol II and hence contribute to enhanced p21 transcription, we performed 3C assays (Fig. 3). In this assay chromatin is cross-linked in living cells as in ChIP assays, but instead of shearing and antibody-based selection, chromatin is restriction digested and then ligated in circumstances favoring intramolecular interactions. Hence the probability that two distant chromatin regions separated by multiple restriction sites will form a ligation product increases, if they are spatially close via either random interactions or specific chromatin looping. We studied the TSS association of five upstream chromatin fragments located 1.5-7 kb from the p21 TSS, where the fragments with location nearest to the TSS should show the highest association based on random interactions (22). Association of the more proximal regions to the TSS was studied using the restriction enzyme Hpy8I, whereas for the more distal regions MvaI was used. To quantify specifically the ligation products of VDRE-containing regions to the TSS of p21, we used FAM-labeled oligonucleotides in quantitative PCR (Fig. 3A).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 64 70 64 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i.e.</italic>
###xml 155 156 151 152 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 157 158 153 154 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 176 177 172 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 170 177 166 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 502 505 498 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 734 739 730 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-1</italic>
###xml 747 748 743 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 741 748 737 744 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 762 767 758 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-1</italic>
###xml 977 978 973 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 971 978 967 974 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1217 1218 1213 1214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1211 1218 1207 1214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1272 1273 1264 1265 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1274 1275 1266 1267 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1380 1381 1372 1373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1374 1381 1366 1373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1447 1448 1439 1440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1441 1448 1433 1440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
MDA-MB453 cells were treated identically as for the ChIP assay (Fig. 2), i.e. the same time points were chosen for chromatin extraction after 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 treatment (Fig. 3B). While the basal looping of the VDRE containing region 2 to the TSS was found to be lower than that of control region 1, as expected based on its location, regions 1 and 3 showed higher association to the TSS than the unresponsive control fragments at -1.5 and -6 kb, respectively. This could indicate active repression of p21 transcription via these regions. Consistently, both NCoR1 and HDAC3 were initially present on these regions and their enrichment decreased ligand-dependently within 15 to 30 min, although VDR was not initially present on region p21-1 (Fig. 2B). For region p21-1, the association with the TSS first decreased at 15 min and was re-introduced at 30 min of ligand treatment. For region 2, the first, albeit minor peak of looping to the TSS was found already at 30 min (Fig. 3B). Interestingly, in this time period the looping of region 3 to the TSS was at its minimum. These observations also fit with the p-Pol II binding at this time point, which showed a maximum for regions 1 and 2, but not for region 3 (Fig. 2B). On all three VDRE-containing regions, 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 maximally induced their association with the TSS by 2-15-fold at 90 min after onset of treatment (Fig. 3B), concomitantly with p-Pol II enrichment on these regions (Fig. 2B).
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 173 174 169 170 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 175 176 171 172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 538 542 534 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21.</italic>
Taken together, basal looping of VDRE containing regions to the TSS correlates with the enrichment of NCoR1 and HDAC3, while the looping after 30 and 90 min of 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 treatment coincides with p-Pol II associations to these regions, suggesting simultaneous looping and transcription initiation. However, at 150 min, the association of the VDRE-containing regions to the TSS is low, although p-Pol II is significantly associated with these regions. This could in principle result from association with TSSs of other genes than of p21. Alternatively, it may suggest that upon loss of ligand-responsive looping, the transcriptional complexes are partitioned to both the TSS and the ligand-responsive regions, explaining enrichment of Pol II on distal regions without association with the TSS.
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 3.</label>
###xml 9 10 9 10 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</bold>
###xml 22 23 18 19 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>

###xml 15 100 11 96 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub> induces dynamic looping of VDR binding regions to the TSS of the <italic>p21</italic> gene.</bold>
###xml 133 136 129 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 185 186 181 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 340 341 336 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 456 457 452 453 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 471 472 463 464 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 473 474 465 466 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 476 477 468 469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 700 711 692 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">left figure</italic>
###xml 765 777 757 769 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right figure</italic>
###xml 815 818 807 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1131 1136 1123 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-2</italic>

###xml 1405 1406 1397 1398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">*</sup>
###xml 1408 1409 1400 1401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 1418 1420 1410 1412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">**</sup>
###xml 1422 1423 1414 1415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>

###xml 9 1543 9 1535 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="40"><bold>1</bold>&#945;<bold>,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub> induces dynamic looping of VDR binding regions to the TSS of the <italic>p21</italic> gene.</bold> Schematic overview on the human <italic>p21</italic> promoter indicating previously described VDREs (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>), MvaI and Hpy81I restriction enzyme recognition sites and location of primers along with FAM-labeled probes used for quantification of the 3C products (<italic>A</italic>). 3C assays were performed with chromatin from MDA-MB453 cells that were treated for the indicated times with 10 n<sc>m</sc> 1&#945;,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub> (<italic>B</italic>). Chromatin was extracted, cross-linked, and digested with either MvaI or Hpy8I. After ligation, the DNA was extracted and analyzed by PCR with primer A in combination with primers C, D, or E for Hpy8I-digested chromatin (<italic>left figure</italic>) or with primers F or G for MvaI-digested chromatin (<italic>right figure</italic>). Re-ligated digestions of subcloned <italic>p21</italic> promoter fragments served as positive controls. Analysis was performed by real-time quantitative PCR using a FAM-labeled probe targeting the ligation site specific for the product. PCR efficacy was normalized to positive controls. Values indicate looping as relative values compared with basal looping of region <italic>p21-2</italic> to the TSS. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's <italic>t</italic> test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (<sup>*</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.05; <sup>**</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.01; <sup>***</sup>, <italic>p</italic> &lt; 0.001). Targeted restriction fragments in <italic>A</italic> and quantitative results in <italic>B</italic> are shown in the same color.</p>

FIGURE 3.1alpha,25(OH)2D3 induces dynamic looping of VDR binding regions to the TSS of the p21 gene. Schematic overview on the human p21 promoter indicating previously described VDREs (6), MvaI and Hpy81I restriction enzyme recognition sites and location of primers along with FAM-labeled probes used for quantification of the 3C products (A). 3C assays were performed with chromatin from MDA-MB453 cells that were treated for the indicated times with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 (B). Chromatin was extracted, cross-linked, and digested with either MvaI or Hpy8I. Data points indicate the means of at least three independent cell treatments, and the bars represent standard deviations. A two-tailed Student's t test was performed to determine the significance of the stimulation in reference to vehicle-treated control (*, p < 0.05; **, p < 0.01; ***, p < 0.001). Targeted restriction fragments in A and quantitative results in B are shown in the same color.

###begin p 40
###xml 0 1 0 1 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</bold>

###xml 6 91 2 87 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">,25(OH)<sub>2</sub>D<sub>3</sub> induces dynamic looping of VDR binding regions to the TSS of the <italic>p21</italic> gene.</bold>
###xml 124 127 120 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 176 177 172 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 331 332 327 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 447 448 443 444 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 462 463 454 455 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 464 465 456 457 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 467 468 459 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>

###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 0 72 0 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">MED1, LSD1, and HDAC4 Are Essential for the Cycling of p21 Transcription</italic>
###xml 221 224 221 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 239 240 239 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 245 246 245 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 231 246 231 246 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2, <italic>B</italic> and <italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 348 349 344 345 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 350 351 346 347 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 423 453 419 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">MED1, HDAC3, HDAC4, CBP, NCoR1</italic>
###xml 459 463 455 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">LSD1</italic>
###xml 522 528 518 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4</xref>
###xml 768 770 764 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 1223 1224 1215 1216 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1225 1226 1217 1218 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1385 1391 1377 1383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1</xref>
MED1, LSD1, and HDAC4 Are Essential for the Cycling of p21 Transcription-Our ChIP results on the ligand-responsive association of co-activators, co-repressors and histone modifying enzymes with the genomic regions of the p21 gene (Fig. 2, B and C) suggest that these proteins have a role in the transcriptional response of the gene to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3. To test this assumption, we individually diminished the expression of MED1, HDAC3, HDAC4, CBP, NCoR1, and LSD1 by siRNA oligonucleotide transfection of MDA-MB453 cells (Fig. 4). Western blot was used to monitor the efficacy of siRNA on the protein level (supplemental Fig. S2). In addition to the factors studied in ChIP assays, we studied the effect of knock-down of VDR-linked cofactors, such as HDAC5 and HDAC7 (17), and the NCoR1 related co-repressor Silencing Mediator of Retinoid and Thyroid Receptors (SMRT, also called NCoR2) in combination with NCoR1 (Fig. S2). The inhibition by specific siRNAs resulted in 15-25% remaining expression of the targeted mRNAs, when compared with cells transfected with non-targeted siRNA (supplemental Fig. S2A). After a 24-h transfection period with siRNA oligonucleotides, the MDA-MB453 cells were stimulated with 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 and RNA was extracted. We focused on the period of 150 to 255 min after the onset of stimulation, which showed the most drastic effects on mRNA accumulation (Fig. 1).
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 201 207 201 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4</xref>
###xml 249 252 249 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 309 312 309 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 501 502 497 498 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 503 504 499 500 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 513 516 509 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 634 637 630 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 650 651 646 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 644 651 640 647 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
We found that knock-down of MED1 totally abolished the transcriptional cycles, validating the essential role of this member of the mediator complex in transmitting the transcriptional response of NRs (Fig. 4). Knock-down of LSD1 decreased the basal p21 mRNA expression and disturbed the cyclical induction of p21 transcript, but did not completely abolish the ligand induced rise in the transcript levels. Knock-down of the other secondary co-activator CBP did not affect either basal or 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 induced p21 gene transcription. This suggests that CBP, despite the ligand-dependent enrichment on the regulatory regions of the p21 gene (Fig. 2B), is unnecessary for the ligand response.
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 122 125 122 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 165 166 161 162 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 167 168 163 164 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 225 228 221 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 291 294 287 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 635 636 627 628 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 637 638 629 630 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 692 694 684 686 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 854 857 846 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 899 902 891 894 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 973 976 965 968 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
Contrary to the co-activator CBP, the reduction of co-repressor expression by siRNA affected both the basal expression of p21 and its responsiveness to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3. The silencing of NCoR1 induced the basal expression of p21 and resulted in shifted timing of the cyclical fluctuation of p21 mRNA upon ligand treatment. Simultaneous silencing of both NCoR1 and SMRT had similar effects on ligand response but lacked effects on basal expression, as did the silencing of TBL1, a member of the NCoR/SMRT silencing complexes. The knock-down of HDACs 3, 4, 5, and 7 (based on our previous studies on their importance in the 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 response of cyclin-dependent kinase inhibitor genes (17)) showed that the roles of individual HDACs in the response were non-redundant and distinct. Knock-down of either HDACs 3, 4, or 5 induced basal expression of p21 and inhibited the ligand-induced rise in p21 transcript level at 150 min. The silencing of HDAC4 lead to disturbed p21 transcript pattern at later time points, whereas the transcript patterns in HDAC3 silenced cells were after 150 min similar to patterns of cells transfected with non-targeted siRNA.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 64 67 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 319 322 319 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 375 376 371 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 377 378 373 374 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
In summary, HDACs and NCoR1 repress the basal expression of the p21 transcript, whereas LSD1 induces it. MED1 is non-redundant and essential to the ligand response, while knock-down of LSD1, HDAC3, HDAC4, or NCoR1 attenuates it. In addition to MED1, silencing of HDAC4 and LSD1 severely disturb the cyclical pattern of p21 transcript accumulation in response to 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 treatment.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 0 79 0 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Histone Dimethylation and Deacetylation Are Indispensable for Chromatin Looping</italic>
###xml 171 172 167 168 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 173 174 169 170 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 210 213 206 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 233 239 229 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4</xref>
###xml 297 298 289 290 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 299 300 291 292 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 339 342 331 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 355 356 347 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 349 356 341 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 571 572 559 560 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 573 574 561 562 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 655 661 643 649 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig. 5</xref>
###xml 702 703 686 687 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 704 705 688 689 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1021 1022 1001 1002 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1023 1024 1003 1004 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
Histone Dimethylation and Deacetylation Are Indispensable for Chromatin Looping-Because the proteins MED1, HDAC4, and LSD1 seem to have a major impact on the 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-dependent cyclical accumulation of p21 transcript levels (Fig. 4) and are ligand-dependently enriched on the 1alpha,25(OH)2D3-responsive regions and the TSS of the p21 gene (Fig. 2B), they might also affect the looping of these regions to the TSS. Therefore, we individually knocked down the expression of MED1, HDAC4, and LSD1 by siRNA in MDA-MB453 cells, stimulated the cells with 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 and performed 3C assays for the association of regions 1, 2 and 3 with the TSS (Fig. 5). On the proximal region 1 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 only mildly induced association to the TSS and the effects of a knock-down of MED1, HDAC4, or LSD1 were not significant. In contrast, the expressions of MED1 and LSD1 were found to be essential for the induction of maximal ligand-induced association between regions 2 and 3 and the TSS after 90 min of 1alpha,25(OH)2D3 treatment. For the ligand-dependent looping between region 3 and the TSS, also HDAC4 showed to be essential. As a reference, the behavior of either of the two control regions was not significantly affected by a knock-down of MED1, HDAC4, or LSD1 (supplemental Fig. S3).
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 4.</label>
###xml 45 48 45 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>

MDA-MB453 cells were transfected for 24 h with siRNA oligonucleotides against the genes MED1, LSD1, HDAC4, NCoR1, HDAC3, CBP, or with a non-targeted siRNA (siCtrl), and subsequently either not stimulated (A) or stimulated (B) for the indicated times with 10 nm 1alpha,25(OH)2D3. ###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 181 184 181 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 218 223 218 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21-3</italic>
In summary, the 3C results after siRNA knock-down suggest that for the bridging of two distal VDR binding chromatin regions to the basal transcriptional machinery on the TSS of the p21 gene, MED1 is indispensable. For p21-3 also HDAC4 is essential for maximal looping to TSS. Moreover, specific demethylation by LSD1 is essential for chromatin looping of even two most distal VDR binding regions.
###end p 48
###begin title 49
DISCUSSION
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 43 46 43 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 167 168 163 164 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 169 170 165 166 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 304 311 300 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 583 586 579 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 717 719 701 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
###xml 721 723 705 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref24">24</xref>
###xml 911 914 895 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 1638 1641 1622 1625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p21</italic>
###xml 692 697 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
In this study, we used the well-known gene p21 as a model to describe how a simple signal, such as the stimulation of MBA-MD453 cells with the VDR ligand 1alpha,25(OH)2D3, can result in cyclicity at the level of transcription factor binding, chromatin looping and eventually transcription (summarized in Table 1). We observed the cyclic responses at high resolution over a time frame of up to 300 min and distinguished an early phase of minor transcriptional induction and a later phase of more pronounced activation, but still modest effects on mRNA induction. Following the peaks, p21 mRNA level decreased rather fast, consistently with previously measured half-life of approximately1 h in human cancer cell lines (23, 24). In the early phase we found two concurrent peaks in VDR and p-Pol II enrichment. The first peak at 30-45 min was preceded by association of MED1 with the VDRE containing regions of the p21 gene. Simultaneous to the second peak in VDR and p-Pol II association at 90 min, looping from the three VDR binding regions to the TSS is 2-15-fold induced allowing physical interaction between the sites. The partially concurrent looping and association of p-Pol II on the distal VDRE containing regions suggests that looping and transcription initiation within a single piece of chromatin are simultaneous events. Whether looping occurs from only one VDRE to the TSS at a time or whether all three VDREs and the TSS connect simultaneously, still remains to be elucidated. These data do not reveal either, whether the elongation of the transcript occurs concurrently with the looping. Consistent with the ChIP results, the p21 transcript accumulation was induced on time points following the peaks in VDR and p-Pol II enrichment.
###end p 50
